# Platform Build Log

Append-only log of work sessions. Each session adds exactly one row, in two edits:

1. **At session start** (before any real work): append a row with status `⏳ IN FLIGHT — {step name}`, commit it immediately as its own standalone commit.
2. **At session end** (after the real work is done, tested, and typechecked): update that same row to `✅ DONE — {step name}`, filling in the real commit hash of the work, then commit the update (either folded into the final commit or immediately after it).

If a session dies, crashes, or is abandoned mid-way, its row stays `⏳ IN FLIGHT`, which is itself the record that an attempt was made and didn't finish.

See [CLAUDE.md](CLAUDE.md) for the exact instructions.

| 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Build Missing Free Checkout Endpoint — POST /api/portal/checkout/free — the marketing site's Checkout.tsx branches free ($0) items (incl. free Assessments, the top-of-funnel product) away from Stripe and POSTs `{ serviceIds, contractIds, guestEmail, captchaToken }` to `/api/portal/checkout/free`, but that endpoint existed NOWHERE in the backend (exhaustive grep, zero matches) — so every free checkout failed at its final step with "Unable to complete registration. Please try again." despite no payment ever being attempted. DISCOVERY: the frontend's PAID twin (`/portal/checkout/create-session` → `/portal/stripe/webhook` → `processStripeEvent`) does full account+project provisioning on success; and a purpose-built FREE-path sibling already existed — `/portal/onboarding/claim-free` (portal.ts:13768, used by the CRM's `OnboardingContract.tsx`) — doing exactly the $0 equivalent, just at a different path the marketing Checkout never called. FIX: extracted claim-free's inline provisioning body into a shared module-level `provisionFreeOnboarding()` helper (returns a discriminated `{ ok, ... } | { ok:false, status, error }` result so callers own HTTP translation), refactored the existing claim-free route into a thin caller of it (behaviour preserved — success `{ ok, sentSetupEmail }`, same status codes; idempotent case now additively returns `sentSetupEmail:false`; guest-missing-email message reworded, still 401), and added the new `POST /portal/checkout/free` route that verifies Turnstile CAPTCHA then calls the same helper. The helper performs the real free-path equivalent of a successful paid checkout: resolves/creates the client account via `ensureClientAccount` (+ `ensureDirectCustomerRecord`/`ensureClientMspUser` for guests), links pre-signed guest contracts (`contractIds`, `isNull(userId)` guard), enforces a server-side `$0` price guard, creates the `quick_win` project + `client_services` (seeding workflow steps + first-step kanban tasks), links each contract→project and attaches its signed PDF as a document, writes deterministic `FREE-ONB-<userId>-<sortedServiceIds>` $0 invoices (idempotency key — retry-safe), sends the account-setup (new accounts) or onboarding-confirmation (returning) email via `sendEmailFromTemplate` (Exchange/Graph, NOT Resend), fires admin SMS/web-push/notification alerts + the `onboarding.free_claimed` workflow event. REUSED vs BUILT: reused the entire claim-free provisioning (now shared, not duplicated) + `verifyCaptchaToken` from `lib/captcha.ts` (same guard as the authenticated offer checkout in `portal-checkout.ts`; transparently bypasses when `TURNSTILE_SECRET_KEY` unset for dev, enforces vs Cloudflare when configured — CAPTCHA NOT weakened); built fresh only the new route wrapper + captcha gate + the `provisionFreeOnboarding` extraction seam. NO Stripe interaction on this path. ALSO FIXED (frontend): Checkout.tsx error panel showed the label "Payment error" even on the free path — now `{service.isFree ? "Registration error" : "Payment error"}` (matches the existing `service.isFree` copy-swap pattern at the Review/pay heading). Frontend request payload + success/failure logic left exactly as-is; backend built to match the confirmed contract (any 2xx = success). VERIFIED: api-server `tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit` — zero errors in portal.ts (only the 5 pre-existing, unrelated `document-generator.ts`/`health-engine.test.ts` errors in unmodified files remain); marketing-site `tsc` exit 0; grep confirmed no test asserts the old claim-free response shape/messages; sed sweep confirmed zero stray `req.`/`res.` refs leaked into the extracted (req/res-less) helper. Not exercised against a live DB (no DATABASE_URL in this env) — verified by full code trace of the request → helper → provisioning chain + clean typecheck. Committed pathspec-scoped (portal.ts + Checkout.tsx only); a concurrent session's dirty `RiskList.tsx` + 7 untracked `design-system/*` component files (Governance visual-enrichment work) were found in the working tree and deliberately LEFT UNTOUCHED, not swept into this commit. | c513427f |

| 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Fix Typewriter Headline Randomization + Repeat Bug — confirmed root cause of both bugs by tracing `useHeroHeadlines.ts` + the seed SQL: `FALLBACK_HEADLINE`'s text is byte-identical to the DB's `sort_order = 0` row (`2026-07-19-hero-headlines.sql`), and the hook seeded `headlines` state to `[FALLBACK_HEADLINE]` (array length 1) before the `/api/public/hero-headlines` fetch resolved. Since `headlineIndex % headlines.length` is always `0 % 1 = 0`, the rotation was trapped on that single entry — typing, pausing, and deleting it in a full loop, potentially more than once — for however long the fetch took; because that entry's text is identical to the real first headline, this was visually indistinguishable from "the first headline plays twice" before the real rotation ever started. Separately, `public-hero.ts` always returned rows `orderBy(asc(sortOrder))` and nothing on the client ever reordered them, so rotation order was always fixed DB order. FIX: added a `loaded` flag set once the fetch settles (success, empty, or failure); while unloaded and still on the 1-element fallback array, the typing effect now holds at the fully-typed fallback instead of deleting/retyping it in a loop. On successful fetch, the headline set is now shuffled once (Fisher-Yates) before being stored, and `headlineIndex`/`charCount`/`phase` are reset so the real rotation starts clean at a random order — not re-shuffled on every cycle, only once per page load. Only `useHeroHeadlines.ts` touched — `Home.tsx`, the admin Hero Headlines management screen, and headline content untouched, per task scope. `shane-mccaw-consulting` typechecks clean (`npx tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit`, exit 0). Not clicked through in a live browser in this environment (no dev server running this session) — verified by full code trace of the fetch → state → effect chain plus the confirmed seed-data match, and clean typecheck. | 2621845e |

| 2026-07-20 | ✅ DONE | Per-Statement SQL Results — the simulator SQL console + manual-migration runner now report each statement in a multi-statement script separately (SSMS-style) instead of only the last statement's result surfacing (Postgres runs the whole batch but node-pg returns only the final result). New `sql-statement-splitter.ts` — a real SQL-aware splitter on top-level semicolons that skips semicolons inside single-quoted literals (`''` escape), double-quoted identifiers (`""` escape), dollar-quoted blocks (`$$`/`$tag$`, with `$1` params correctly NOT treated as dollar quotes), `--` line comments, and nestable `/* */` block comments; keeps a trailing unterminated statement; drops whitespace/comment-only segments; leaves BEGIN/COMMIT as their own statements so wrapped scripts replay correctly. 16 unit tests (added to the hardcoded vitest include list) cover every case, all green. `executeRawSql()` rewritten: splits the script, runs each statement in its own `client.query()` round-trip on a SINGLE `pool.connect()` connection (so a `BEGIN;…;COMMIT;` script genuinely shares one transaction), catches errors per-statement so statement N failing doesn't stop N+1, and returns `{ statements: [{ statementIndex, statementText (≤500-char preview), success, rows, rowCount, fields, executionMs, error? }] }`; a best-effort `ROLLBACK` in `finally` guarantees a half-open/aborted transaction is never handed back to the pool (no-op warning otherwise). Both call sites (`/simulator/sql/execute`, `/simulator/migrations/execute`) inherit the new array shape unchanged. Frontend `SqlQueryOutput.tsx` reshaped from a single result view to one collapsible block per statement — each with its own success/error icon, `#N` index, truncated statement preview, row count or inline error, and timing; failed statements render their error on their own block (not page-level) so the rest stay readable; the TABLE/JSON toggle now applies per block. `SqlOutput`/type reshaped (`results` → `statements[]`) in `SqlQueryCanvas.tsx`; toolbar shows `N stmts · Xms · Y failed`. The server re-validates the id against listRemediableOffers before returning proposedRemediation, so a hallucinated/ineligible id (or ANY marker from a non-testbed tenant, whose list is empty) yields no actionable proposal; marker is stripped from the visible reply. support-chat.tsx renders an explicit Confirm & run / Not now card — only a human click calls the real endpoint; its 403 for non-testbed is surfaced honestly (no silent fail, no false success). Greeting/disclaimer copy updated (was "I can't take actions"). | 2026-07-19 | ✅ DONE | Dashboard Export + Share Link — D1 DECISION: both features render a frozen point-in-time snapshot, not a live view, matching the precedent set by the existing document-sharing feature (its public view also serves htmlContent captured at generation time, not a live re-render) — an unauthenticated *live* dashboard view would mean exposing the resolver data path with no auth, a materially bigger security surface, for a "share this" feature that doesn't need it. Threshold: 5 failed passwords within a 15-minute window locks the account for 15 minutes (ACCOUNT_LOCKOUT_THRESHOLD/_WINDOW_MINUTES/_DURATION_MINUTES env-overridable, hardcoded defaults otherwise) — chosen as a standard, conservative anti-brute-force default; deliberately looser than the existing per-IP loginLimiter (10/15min) since this is a second, per-account layer, not a replacement. /auth/login now checks lockedUntil before the bcrypt compare (blocks with 423 + accountLocked:true, no password-validity signal leaked) and increments/locks on each bad password (423 the moment the threshold is crossed) — mirrors the mfaEnforced pattern of returning before token issuance, both now sharing one consolidated mspUsersTable lookup instead of two. AUDIT-FIRST findings, all verified directly against current Microsoft Learn API reference (2025-11/2026-02 revisions), not guessed: (1) isolate = `POST https://api.security.microsoft.com/api/machines/{id}/isolate`, body `{ Comment (required), IsolationType: "Full"|"Selective"|"UnManagedDevice" }`, Application permission `Machine.Isolate`; (2) release-from-isolation = `POST .../unisolate`, body `{ Comment }`, same `Machine.Isolate` permission; (3) run-AV-scan = `POST .../runAntiVirusScan`, body `{ Comment (required), ScanType: "Quick"|"Full" }`, Application permission `Machine.Scan` (confirmed the real permission name — NOT a guessed "Machine.RunAntivirus"). All three return 201 Created + a MachineAction resource (typed). These permissions are granted under the **WindowsDefenderATP** API surface in the app registration, SEPARATE from Microsoft Graph — so documented them in a new exported `REQUIRED_DEFENDER_APP_PERMISSIONS` const in this file, deliberately NOT added to graph.ts's `REQUIRED_MT_SCOPES` (that is the Graph `.default` consent set; mixing a non-Graph scope in would break Graph token acquisition), with a comment that adding them forces fresh admin re-consent on every tenant. CRITICAL TOKEN-AUDIENCE GOTCHA baked in with a citing comment (Microsoft's own docs): the token scope is the LEGACY resource `https://api.securitycenter.microsoft.com/.default` even though the request host is `api.security.microsoft.com` — a mismatched audience returns 403 even against the right endpoint; do not "fix" the mismatch. Regional host variants (`us.`/`eu.`) overridable via `DEFENDER_ENDPOINT_API_BASE` env without a code change. DELIBERATE DESIGN DECISION (operational-risk-driven): Defender consent errors throw a dedicated `DefenderConsentError` and do NOT call graph.ts's `markTenantConsentRevoked` — Defender permission consent is a SEPARATE consent surface from the shared Graph `tenant_consent` row, and a tenant with valid Graph consent but no Defender re-consent returns AADSTS65001; flipping the Graph consent row there would wrongly disable working Graph monitoring (the exact collateral damage this integration must avoid). This layer evicts only its own token cache. All three write functions require a non-empty operator `Comment` (Microsoft requires it + it is Defender's audit trail); 403-insufficient-privilege / 409-conflict / "already in progress" / 404 surfaced as typed non-throwing results, only re-consent and network errors propagate. `integration.defender` added as a new leaf channel under the existing `integration.*` taxonomy (task-sanctioned). Documented 100 calls/min + 1,500/hr rate limits in a comment; no rate-limiting infra built (out of scope) — just a "don't call in a tight loop" note. api-server typechecks clean (only the pre-existing `health-engine.test.ts` TS2698 debt remains, consistent with prior sessions; zero Defender-related errors). | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Investigate --text-secondary Token Contrast — real-device feedback (screenshot) showed text still reading too dark/low-contrast even where components correctly use `text-secondary` (confirmed via code read, e.g. `DeliverablesList.tsx`), despite the token passing WCAG AA on paper. Root cause: the token's own color value, not misapplied classes — prior audit already confirmed correct class usage everywhere. Calculated real contrast ratios (WCAG relative-luminance formula, Node) for `--rebuild-text-secondary` against both `--charcoal-0` (`#1A1A1C`) and `--charcoal-1` (`#232326`): old `#9A9AA3` = 6.23:1 / 5.62:1 (AA pass, AAA fail on charcoal-1). Tested a ladder of brighter candidates and picked `#B5B5BC` = 8.52:1 / 7.69:1 — clears AAA (7:1) on both backgrounds, keeps the same cool-neutral hue ratio (B-channel ~7-9 above R/G, matching the original's tint) so it reads as the same color family just brighter, and stays a clear step below `--text-primary` (`#F5F5F7`, ~14:1) so the secondary/primary hierarchy is preserved — not pure white.
